## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task models the temporal evolution of a biological population, where the growth rate depends on current population size and time. It belongs to mathematical biology and theoretical ecology, focusing on density-dependent regulation, environmental forcing, and demographic feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted exponential population increase)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (decelerating growth with asymptotic carrying capacity)
- Ricker model: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (overcompensatory density dependence)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (reduced per-capita growth at low densities)
- Seasonal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental modulation of birth/death rates)
- Time-varying resources: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(-c2 * t)) (carrying capacity changing exponentially over time)
- Higher-order density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (complex intraspecific competition and resource depletion)
- Beverton-Holt continuous form: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (recruitment saturation at high population densities)
- Threshold-dependent recruitment: dP_dt = c0 * P * Max(P - c1, 0) / (P + c2) (strong Allee effect combined with density saturation)
- Gamma-type temporal response: dP_dt = c0 * P * t**c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (time-lagged population bloom and subsequent decline)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Intraspecific competition → Negative quadratic or cubic terms in population (-c*P**2, -c*P**3) representing resource limitation
- Allee effect / critical depensation → Growth rate increases with P at low densities → P*(P-c1) or P**2 dominance
- Seasonal environmental forcing → Sinusoidal modulation of intrinsic parameters → sin(c*t), cos(c*t)
- Overcompensatory dynamics → Exponential suppression with population size → P*exp(-c*P), often preceding oscillations
- Asymptotic saturation via feedback → Logarithmic regulation → P*(c1 - log(P)) for smooth deceleration
- Time-dependent carrying capacity → Exponential or polynomial time scaling → P*(1 + c*t**2) or P*exp(-c*t)
- Harvesting or exploitation pressure → Linear subtraction proportional to population or effort → -c*P or -c*t*P

The user wants me to identify which of the 51 candidates mathematically equate to the Ground Truth (GT).

**Ground Truth Analysis:**
GT symbolic expression: `c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - exp(-c7*P))*P`
GT numerical expression: `0.8450821034088298*(-1 + P/5.115386454523557)*(1 - P/34.43886242377677)*P + 0.8450821034088298*(1 - exp(-0.09687266473516928*P))*P`
Variables: `t`, `P`. Note that `t` does not appear in the GT expression. It's a function of `P` only.
Let's expand the GT expression to understand its structure.
Term 1: `c0 * (-c1 + P/c2) * (c3 - P/c4) * P`
This is a cubic polynomial in `P`.
Let's expand `(-c1 + P/c2) * (c3 - P/c4)`:
`= -c1*c3 + c1*P/c4 + c3*P/c2 - P^2/(c2*c4)`
Multiply by `c0 * P`:
`= c0 * (-c1*c3*P + (c1/c4 + c3/c2)*P^2 - 1/(c2*c4)*P^3)`
So Term 1 is a cubic polynomial in `P` with no constant term.

Term 2: `c5 * (c6 - exp(-c7*P)) * P`
`= c5*c6*P - c5*P*exp(-c7*P)`
This is a linear term in `P` plus a term involving `P * exp(-c7*P)`.

So the GT function is of the form:
`f(P) = a*P^3 + b*P^2 + d*P + e*P*exp(-k*P)`
where `a, b, d, e, k` are constants derived from `c0..c7`.
Specifically:
`a = -c0 / (c2*c4)`
`b = c0 * (c1/c4 + c3/c2)`
`d = -c0*c1*c3 + c5*c6`
`e = -c5`
`k = c7`

So the GT is a cubic polynomial in `P` (with zero constant term) plus a term `P * exp(-c7*P)`.
Wait, `P * exp(-c7*P)` is not a polynomial. It's a transcendental function.
So the GT has basis functions: `P`, `P^2`, `P^3`, and `P * exp(-c7*P)`.
Actually, `P * exp(-c7*P)` can be written as `P * exp(c * P)` where `c = -c7`.
So the GT is a linear combination of `P`, `P^2`, `P^3`, and `P * exp(c * P)`.

Let's check the candidates. They are mostly combinations of polynomials, exponentials, logs, sines, etc.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - exp(-c7*P))*P`
Expanding the first term yields a cubic polynomial in `P` with no constant term: `A*P^3 + B*P^2 + C*P`.
The second term expands to `D*P - E*P*exp(-c7*P)`, which combines with the linear term to form `F*P - E*P*exp(-c7*P)`.
Thus, the GT function has the exact functional form:
`f(P) = a*P^3 + b*P^2 + d*P + e*P*exp(k*P)`
where `a, b, d, e, k` are arbitrary real constants derived from the GT parameters. Any matching candidate must be able to represent this exact combination of basis functions: `P^3`, `P^2`, `P`, and `P*exp(c*P)`.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG3)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - exp(-c7*P))*P
Candidates evaluated: 51
Matched candidate IDs: [14, 39]
Matched candidates: ["P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + c3*exp(P*c4) + c5)", "P*(c0*exp(P*c1) + c2*(P + c3)*(P + c4))"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
```
0.845*(−1 + P/5.115)*(1 − P/34.44)*P + 0.845*(1 − exp(−0.0969*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `0.845*(P/5.115 − 1)*(1 − P/34.44)*P`
  - `= 0.845*(P/5.115 − P²/(5.115*34.44) − 1 + P/34.44)*P`
  - `= 0.845*P*(P/5.115 + P/34.44 − P²/176.13 − 1)`
  - `= 0.845*P*((34.44+5.115)P/176.13 − P²/176.13 − 1)`
  - `= 0.845*P*(39.555P/176.13 − P²/176.13 − 1)`
  - `= 0.845*P*(0.2246P − 0.005678P² − 1)`

- Second term: `0.845*(1 − exp(−0.0969*P))*P = 0.845*P − 0.845*P*exp(−0.0969*P)`

Combining:
```
GT = 0.845*P*(0.2246P − 0.005678P² − 1) + 0.845*P − 0.845*P*exp(−0.0969*P)
   = 0.845*P*(0.2246P − 0.005678P² − 1 + 1) − 0.845*P*exp(−0.0969*P)
   = 0.845*P*(0.2246P − 0.005678P²) − 0.845*P*exp(−0.0969*P)
   = 0.845*(0.2246*P² − 0.005678*P³) − 0.845*P*exp(−0.0969*P)
```

So GT simplifies to:
```
GT = a*P² + b*P³ + c*P*exp(d*P)
```
where a = 0.845*0.2246 ≈ 0.1898, b = −0.845*0.005678 ≈ −0.004798, c = −0.845, d = −0.0969.

**The GT has the form: P³*(const) + P²*(const) + P*exp(negative*P)*(const)**

This means the basis functions are: {P³, P², P·exp(α·P)} where α < 0.

Now let me check each candidate against this structure.

**Candidate 1:** `P*c0*(P+c1)*(P+c2) + c3*cos(c4*exp(P*c5))`
= c0*P*(P²+(c1+c2)P+c1c2) + c3*cos(c4*exp(c5*P))
= c0*P³ + ... + cos(exp(P)) term. The cos(exp(P)) is not equivalent to P*exp(αP). **[NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 2-4, 6, 16, 19, 40, 43, 47-50:** These contain sin/cos terms. The GT has no trigonometric functions; it has P*exp(αP). Sin cannot equal P*exp(αP). **[NO MATCH]** for all.
